Observer-Pattern component that passively collects model-level\n *        performance metrics and proactively triggers automated retraining\n *        jobs when statistically significant model drift is detected.\n *\n *  Usage:\n *      #define LEXILEARN_RETRAINING_TRIGGER_IMPLEMENTATION\n *      #include \"retraining_trigger.h\"\n *\n *  The first translation unit that defines\n *      LEXILEARN_RETRAINING_TRIGGER_IMPLEMENTATION\n *  gets the function definitions; every other TU only sees the declarations.\n *\n *  Thread-safety:  All public APIs are thread-safe and can be called from the\n *                  metrics-logging hot-path as well as from the scheduler.\n *\n *  Copyright (c) 2024  LexiLearn\n */\n\n#ifndef LEXILEARN_RETRAINING_TRIGGER_H\n#define LEXILEARN_RETRAINING_TRIGGER_H\n\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------\n *  Public Dependencies\n * -------------------------------------------------------------------------*/\n#include <stdbool.h>\n#include <stddef.h>\n#include <stdint.h>\n\n#ifdef __cplusplus\nextern \"C\" {\n#endif\n\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------\n *  Compile-time Configuration\n * -------------------------------------------------------------------------*/\n#ifndef RT_MAX_MODELS\n#define RT_MAX_MODELS          64      /* maximum number of concurrently-tracked models */\n#endif\n\n#ifndef RT_MAX_SAMPLES\n#define RT_MAX_SAMPLES         32      /* sliding window size per model */\n#endif\n\n#ifndef RT_BASELINE_WINDOW\n#define RT_BASELINE_WINDOW      5      /* number of initial samples to establish baseline */\n#endif\n\n#ifndef RT_MODEL_ID_MAX\n#define RT_MODEL_ID_MAX        64      /* bytes incl.\\ null-terminator */\n#endif\n\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------\n *  Status / Error Codes\n * -------------------------------------------------------------------------*/\ntypedef enum\n{\n    RT_OK = 0,\n    RT_ERR_FULL,            /* registry full \u2013 no free slots              */\n    RT_ERR_NOT_FOUND,       /* model not registered                        */\n    RT_ERR_ALREADY_EXISTS,  /* model already registered                    */\n    RT_ERR_BAD_PARAM,       /* null ptr / invalid argument                 */\n    RT_ERR_INTERNAL         /* unexpected internal failure                 */\n} rt_status_t;\n\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------\n *  Metric Descriptor\n * -------------------------------------------------------------------------*/\ntypedef enum\n{\n    RT_METRIC_ACCURACY,\n    RT_METRIC_LOSS,\n    RT_METRIC_ROUGE,\n    RT_METRIC_F1,\n    RT_METRIC_CUSTOM\n} rt_metric_t;\n\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------\n *  Callback Signature\n * -------------------------------------------------------------------------*/\n/*\n *  The orchestrator registers exactly one callback that gets invoked\n *  whenever drift is detected for a given model.  The callback must return\n *  true on success so that the trigger can reset its \u201cretraining pending\u201d\n *  flag; returning false keeps the flag set and the trigger will retry once\n *  per check-interval (the orchestrator may choose to back-off).\n */\ntypedef bool (*rt_retrain_callback_t)(const char *model_id);\n\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------\n *  Public API\n * -------------------------------------------------------------------------*/\n\n/* Initialization / shutdown */\nrt_status_t rt_trigger_init(rt_retrain_callback_t cb);\nvoid        rt_trigger_shutdown(void);\n\n/* Model-level registry management */\nrt_status_t rt_register_model(const char *model_id,\n                              rt_metric_t metric,\n                              double drift_threshold_pct);  /* e.g. 5.0 for 5 % */\n\nrt_status_t rt_unregister_model(const char *model_id);\n\n/* Metric ingestion (hot-path) */\nrt_status_t rt_record_metric(const char *model_id,\n                             double      value,             /* raw metric value */\n                             uint64_t    timestamp_ms);     /* epoch millis     */\n\n/* Synchronous check \u2013 can be called by cron-like job every N minutes */\nvoid rt_check_and_schedule(void);\n\n/* Poll whether the last check flagged a model for retraining. Mainly for unit-tests. */\nbool rt_has_pending_retraining(const char *model_id);\n\n#ifdef __cplusplus\n}\n#endif\n\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------*/\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------*/\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------*/\n/*              Implementation \u2013 only if requested by compile unit          */\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------*/\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------*/\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------*/\n#ifdef LEXILEARN_RETRAINING_TRIGGER_IMPLEMENTATION\n\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------\n *  Private Includes\n * -------------------------------------------------------------------------*/\n#include <pthread.h>\n#include <stdlib.h>\n#include <string.h>\n#include <time.h>\n\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------\n *  Private Helper Macros\n * -------------------------------------------------------------------------*/\n#define RT_MIN(a,b) ((a) < (b) ? (a) : (b))\n#define RT_MAX(a,b) ((a) > (b) ? (a) : (b))\n\n/* Return current time in milliseconds since epoch \u2013 for internal bookkeeping\n * when caller passes 0 for timestamp_ms.\n */\nstatic uint64_t _rt_now_ms(void)\n{\n    struct timespec ts;\n    clock_gettime(CLOCK_REALTIME, &ts);\n    return ((uint64_t) ts.tv_sec) * 1000ULL + (uint64_t) (ts.tv_nsec / 1000000ULL);\n}\n\n/* Metric ring-buffer element */\ntypedef struct\n{\n    double   value;\n    uint64_t ts_ms;\n} rt_sample_t;\n\n/* Model registry entry */\ntypedef struct\n{\n    bool             in_use;\n    char             model_id[RT_MODEL_ID_MAX];\n\n    /* configuration */\n    rt_metric_t      metric_type;\n    double           drift_threshold_pct;   /* % drop/increase vs baseline */\n\n    /* runtime state */\n    rt_sample_t      samples[RT_MAX_SAMPLES];\n    size_t           head;                  /* next insertion point */\n    size_t           count;                 /* current number of samples */\n    bool             retrain_pending;       /* drift detected, waiting for handler */\n} rt_model_entry_t;\n\n/* Global registry */\nstatic struct\n{\n    pthread_mutex_t      mtx;\n    rt_model_entry_t     entries[RT_MAX_MODELS];\n    rt_retrain_callback_t callback;\n    bool                 initialized;\n} _rt_state = {\n    .mtx          = PTHREAD_MUTEX_INITIALIZER,\n    .entries      = { {0} },\n    .callback     = NULL,\n    .initialized  = false\n};\n\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------\n *  Internal Functions\n * -------------------------------------------------------------------------*/\n\n/* Thread-safe lookup (caller must hold lock) */\nstatic rt_model_entry_t *_rt_find_entry(const char *model_id)\n{\n    for (size_t i = 0; i < RT_MAX_MODELS; ++i)\n    {\n        if (_rt_state.entries[i].in_use &&\n            strncmp(_rt_state.entries[i].model_id, model_id, RT_MODEL_ID_MAX) == 0)\n        {\n            return &_rt_state.entries[i];\n        }\n    }\n    return NULL;\n}\n\n/* Compute average of N most recent samples from ring buffer */\nstatic double _rt_avg_last_n(const rt_model_entry_t *ent, size_t n)\n{\n    if (ent->count == 0) { return 0.0; }\n    n = RT_MIN(n, ent->count);\n    double sum = 0.0;\n    for (size_t i = 0; i < n; ++i)\n    {\n        size_t idx = (ent->head + RT_MAX_SAMPLES - 1 - i) % RT_MAX_SAMPLES;\n        sum += ent->samples[idx].value;\n    }\n    return sum / (double) n;\n}\n\n/* Compute baseline average consisting of the oldest N samples */\nstatic double _rt_avg_first_n(const rt_model_entry_t *ent, size_t n)\n{\n    if (ent->count == 0) { return 0.0; }\n    n = RT_MIN(n, ent->count);\n    double sum = 0.0;\n    size_t start = (ent->head + RT_MAX_SAMPLES - ent->count) % RT_MAX_SAMPLES;\n    for (size_t i = 0; i < n; ++i)\n    {\n        size_t idx = (start + i) % RT_MAX_SAMPLES;\n        sum += ent->samples[idx].value;\n    }\n    return sum / (double) n;\n}\n\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------\n *  Public API \u2013 Implementation\n * -------------------------------------------------------------------------*/\nrt_status_t rt_trigger_init(rt_retrain_callback_t cb)\n{\n    if (cb == NULL) { return RT_ERR_BAD_PARAM; }\n\n    pthread_mutex_lock(&_rt_state.mtx);\n    _rt_state.callback    = cb;\n    _rt_state.initialized = true;\n    pthread_mutex_unlock(&_rt_state.mtx);\n\n    return RT_OK;\n}\n\nvoid rt_trigger_shutdown(void)\n{\n    pthread_mutex_lock(&_rt_state.mtx);\n    memset(_rt_state.entries, 0, sizeof(_rt_state.entries));\n    _rt_state.callback    = NULL;\n    _rt_state.initialized = false;\n    pthread_mutex_unlock(&_rt_state.mtx);\n}\n\nrt_status_t rt_register_model(const char *model_id,\n                              rt_metric_t metric,\n                              double drift_threshold_pct)\n{\n    if (!model_id || drift_threshold_pct <= 0.0) { return RT_ERR_BAD_PARAM; }\n\n    rt_status_t status = RT_ERR_FULL;\n    pthread_mutex_lock(&_rt_state.mtx);\n\n    /* duplicate? */\n    if (_rt_find_entry(model_id) != NULL)\n    {\n        status = RT_ERR_ALREADY_EXISTS;\n        goto out;\n    }\n\n    /* locate free slot */\n    for (size_t i = 0; i < RT_MAX_MODELS; ++i)\n    {\n        if (!_rt_state.entries[i].in_use)\n        {\n            rt_model_entry_t *ent = &_rt_state.entries[i];\n            memset(ent, 0, sizeof(*ent));\n            ent->in_use              = true;\n            ent->metric_type         = metric;\n            ent->drift_threshold_pct = drift_threshold_pct;\n            strncpy(ent->model_id, model_id, RT_MODEL_ID_MAX - 1);\n            status = RT_OK;\n            goto out;\n        }\n    }\n\nout:\n    pthread_mutex_unlock(&_rt_state.mtx);\n    return status;\n}\n\nrt_status_t rt_unregister_model(const char *model_id)\n{\n    if (!model_id) { return RT_ERR_BAD_PARAM; }\n\n    pthread_mutex_lock(&_rt_state.mtx);\n    rt_model_entry_t *ent = _rt_find_entry(model_id);\n    if (ent)\n    {\n        memset(ent, 0, sizeof(*ent));\n        pthread_mutex_unlock(&_rt_state.mtx);\n        return RT_OK;\n    }\n    pthread_mutex_unlock(&_rt_state.mtx);\n    return RT_ERR_NOT_FOUND;\n}\n\nrt_status_t rt_record_metric(const char *model_id,\n                             double      value,\n                             uint64_t    timestamp_ms)\n{\n    if (!model_id) { return RT_ERR_BAD_PARAM; }\n    if (timestamp_ms == 0) { timestamp_ms = _rt_now_ms(); }\n\n    pthread_mutex_lock(&_rt_state.mtx);\n    rt_model_entry_t *ent = _rt_find_entry(model_id);\n    if (!ent)\n    {\n        pthread_mutex_unlock(&_rt_state.mtx);\n        return RT_ERR_NOT_FOUND;\n    }\n\n    /* insert into ring buffer */\n    ent->samples[ent->head].value  = value;\n    ent->samples[ent->head].ts_ms  = timestamp_ms;\n    ent->head   = (ent->head + 1) % RT_MAX_SAMPLES;\n    ent->count  = RT_MIN(ent->count + 1, RT_MAX_SAMPLES);\n\n    pthread_mutex_unlock(&_rt_state.mtx);\n    return RT_OK;\n}\n\n/* Determine drift for a single entry (lock must be held) */\nstatic bool _rt_drift_detected(rt_model_entry_t *ent)\n{\n    if (ent->count < RT_BASELINE_WINDOW * 2) { return false; }\n\n    double baseline = _rt_avg_first_n(ent, RT_BASELINE_WINDOW);\n    double current  = _rt_avg_last_n(ent,  RT_BASELINE_WINDOW);\n\n    if (baseline == 0.0) { return false; } /* avoid div-by-zero */\n\n    double delta_pct;\n    if (ent->metric_type == RT_METRIC_LOSS)\n    {\n        /* increase in loss indicates drift */\n        delta_pct = ((current - baseline) / baseline) * 100.0;\n        return delta_pct >= ent->drift_threshold_pct;\n    }\n    else\n    {\n        /* decrease in metric (accuracy, F1, etc.) indicates drift */\n        delta_pct = ((baseline - current) / baseline) * 100.0;\n        return delta_pct >= ent->drift_threshold_pct;\n    }\n}\n\nvoid rt_check_and_schedule(void)\n{\n    if (!_rt_state.initialized || !_rt_state.callback) { return; }\n\n    pthread_mutex_lock(&_rt_state.mtx);\n\n    /* scan registry */\n    for (size_t i = 0; i < RT_MAX_MODELS; ++i)\n    {\n        rt_model_entry_t *ent = &_rt_state.entries[i];\n        if (!ent->in_use || ent->retrain_pending) { continue; }\n\n        if (_rt_drift_detected(ent))\n        {\n            ent->retrain_pending = true;\n            /* Unlock during callback to avoid deadlocks */\n            pthread_mutex_unlock(&_rt_state.mtx);\n            bool ok = _rt_state.callback(ent->model_id);\n            pthread_mutex_lock(&_rt_state.mtx);\n\n            if (ok)\n            {\n                /* Callback accepted the scheduling \u2013 reset samples to establish new baseline */\n                ent->count            = 0;\n                ent->head             = 0;\n                ent->retrain_pending  = false;\n            }\n            /* else: keep pending flag set for future retries */\n        }\n    }\n\n    pthread_mutex_unlock(&_rt_state.mtx);\n}\n\nbool rt_has_pending_retraining(const char *model_id)\n{\n    if (!model_id) { return false; }\n    bool pending = false;\n    pthread_mutex_lock(&_rt_state.mtx);\n    rt_model_entry_t *ent = _rt_find_entry(model_id);\n    if (ent) { pending = ent->retrain_pending; }\n    pthread_mutex_unlock(&_rt_state.mtx);\n    return pending;\n}\n\n#endif /* LEXILEARN_RETRAINING_TRIGGER_IMPLEMENTATION */\n#endif /* LEXILEARN_RETRAINING_TRIGGER_H */\n",

Optional\n *  operations (e.g. load/save) may return LEXI_ERR_NOT_IMPLEMENTED when\n *  unsupported.\n */\ntypedef struct model_strategy_vtable\n{\n    /*\n     *  configure():\n     *      Apply a list of hyper-parameters prior to training.\n     *\n     *  Return:\n     *      LEXI_OK on success, or appropriate error code.\n     */\n    lexi_status_t (*configure)(model_strategy_t      *self,\n                               const hyperparam_t    *params,\n                               size_t                 param_count);\n\n    /*\n     *  train():\n     *      Fit the model to the given datasets. Must free all memory and release GPU/CPU handles.\n     */\n    void (*destroy)(model_strategy_t *self);\n\n} model_strategy_vtable_t;\n\n/*---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n * Registry API\n *  \u2013 Facilitates dynamic discovery and instantiation of strategies\n *---------------------------------------------------------------------------*/\n\n/* Prototype that concrete strategies must expose */\ntypedef model_strategy_t *(*strategy_ctor_fn)(void);\n\n/*\n *  ll_strategy_register():\n *      Register a constructor under a unique, case-insensitive name.\n *\n *  Typical usage (inside transformer_summarizer.c):\n *      static model_strategy_t *transformer_ctor(void) { \u2026 }\n *      __attribute__((constructor))\n *      static void _init(void)\n *      {\n *          ll_strategy_register(\"transformer_summarizer\", transformer_ctor);\n *      }\n */\nlexi_status_t ll_strategy_register(const char      *name,\n                                   strategy_ctor_fn ctor);\n\n/*\n *  ll_strategy_create():\n *      Instantiate a strategy by name.  Caller owns the returned pointer and\n *      must eventually invoke ->vptr->destroy().\n */\nmodel_strategy_t *ll_strategy_create(const char *name);\n\n/*\n *  ll_strategy_list():\n *      Enumerate all names currently registered.   "content": "# LexiLearn MVC Orchestrator: Architectural Analysis and Critique\n\n**Document Type:** Onboarding Guide for Senior Developers\n**Version:** 1.0\n**Author:** Architecture Team\n**Date:** 2024\n\n---\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nThis document provides a definitive guide to the LexiLearn MVC Orchestrator's architecture, a C-based system for managing NLP/ML model pipelines with automated retraining, monitoring, and versioning. The system unconventionally applies the Model-View-Controller (MVC) pattern to an ML orchestration domain. This guide maps the components to MVC roles, describes communication pathways, traces a critical workflow, and provides a balanced architectural critique.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Component Mapping to MVC Roles\n\nThe LexiLearn Orchestrator implements a clear MVC pattern through its directory structure and component responsibilities. Below is the mapping with justifications:\n\n### 1.1 Model Layer (`src/model/`)\n\nThe **Model** layer encapsulates all machine learning and data-related logic. It is completely agnostic to orchestration concerns and can operate independently.\n\n| Directory/Component | File(s) | Purpose & Role |\n|---------------------|---------|----------------|\n| **Preprocessing** | `text_cleaner.{c,h}`, `tokenizer.{c,h}` | Text normalization and tokenization (BPE, WordPiece, SentencePiece) |\n| **ML Models** | `model_strategy.h`, `transformer_summarizer.{c,h}`, `ngram_analyzer.{c,h}`, `hybrid_model.{c,h}` | Strategy Pattern implementations for pluggable algorithms |\n| **ML Pipeline** | `model_trainer.{c,h}`, `model_evaluator.{c,h}`, `experiment_tracker.{c,h}` | Training orchestration, metrics computation, experiment tracking |\n| **Model Registry** | `model_registry.{c,h}` | SQLite-backed versioning, lifecycle management (EXPERIMENT \u2192 STAGING \u2192 PRODUCTION \u2192 ARCHIVED), model lineage |\n| **Feature Store** | `feature_store_manager.{c,h}` | Versioned feature storage and retrieval |\n\n**Justification:** The Model layer contains:\n- All domain-specific ML logic (training, inference, evaluation)\n- Data persistence (Model Registry)\n- No knowledge of scheduling, monitoring, or presentation concerns\n- Pure business logic that could theoretically be extracted into a library\n\nThe `model_strategy.h` file (`src/model/ml_models/model_strategy.h:96-173`) defines the Strategy Pattern vtable:\n\n```c\ntypedef struct model_strategy_vtable {\n    lexi_status_t (*configure)(model_strategy_t *self, const hyperparam_t *params, size_t param_count);\n    lexi_status_t (*train)(model_strategy_t *self, const ll_dataset_t *training_data, ...);\n    lexi_status_t (*predict)(model_strategy_t *self, const ll_dataset_t *input_data, ...);\n    lexi_status_t (*evaluate)(model_strategy_t *self, const ll_dataset_t *test_data, double *out_score);\n    lexi_status_t (*save)(model_strategy_t *self, const char *artifact_uri);\n    lexi_status_t (*load)(model_strategy_t *self, const char *artifact_uri);\n    void (*destroy)(model_strategy_t *self);\n} model_strategy_vtable_t;\n```\n\n### 1.2 View Layer (`src/view/`)\n\nThe **View** layer handles all presentation and external communication concerns.\n\n| Component | File(s) | Purpose & Role |\n|-----------|---------|----------------|\n| **Dashboard Server** | `dashboard_server.{c,h}` | HTTP/WebSocket server for real-time dashboards, metrics streaming, educator control panels |\n\n**Justification:** The View layer:\n- Exposes REST endpoints (e.g., `/api/retrain`) for manual interventions\n- Provides WebSocket channels for real-time metric push to dashboards\n- Handles TLS/HTTPS, CORS, and client connection management\n- Contains no ML logic\u2014purely concerned with presenting data and accepting user commands\n\nFrom `dashboard_server.h:85-91`:\n```c\ntypedef int (*dashboard_route_cb)(\n    const char *uri,\n    const char *request_body,\n    size_t request_len,\n    char **response_body,\n    size_t *response_len,\n    void *user_ctx);\n```\n\n### 1.3 Controller Layer (`src/controller/`)\n\nThe **Controller** layer orchestrates the entire system, mediating between Model and View.\n\n| Directory/Component | File(s) | Purpose & Role |\n|---------------------|---------|----------------|\n| **Orchestrator** | `orchestrator.{c,h}` | Central command center coordinating the entire MLOps pipeline |\n| **Pipeline** | `pipeline_manager.{c,h}`, `ingestion_stage.{c,h}`, `training_stage.{c,h}`, `deployment_stage.{c,h}` | Pipeline Pattern for ETL \u2192 Training \u2192 Deployment |\n| **Job Factory** | `job_factory.{c,h}`, `job_types.h` | Factory Pattern for creating diverse training jobs |\n| **Monitoring** | `model_monitor.{c,h}`, `drift_detector.{c,h}`, `observer.h`, `retraining_trigger.{c,h}` | Drift detection, Observer Pattern for events, automated retraining triggers |\n| **Scheduler** | `task_scheduler.{c,h}` | Cron-like scheduling for automated tasks |\n\n**Justification:** The Controller layer:\n- Coordinates workflow between Model and View\n- Makes decisions about when to retrain, what strategy to use\n- Contains no ML algorithms\u2014delegates to Model layer\n- Contains no presentation logic\u2014delegates to View layer\n- Implements the Observer Pattern to decouple drift detection from retraining\n\nFrom `orchestrator.c:165-257`, the `start_training_pipeline()` function shows the Controller coordinating Model components:\n```c\n// 1. Ingest \u2192 2. Preprocess \u2192 3. Hyperparameter Tuning \u2192 4. Train via Factory \u2192 5. Register \u2192 6. Notify\n```\n\n---\n\n## 2. Communication Pathways and Data Flow\n\n### 2.1 High-Level Communication Architecture\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502                           MVC Orchestrator                                  \u2502\n\u2502  \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510  uses   \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510  uses   \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510                    \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502 2.2 Controller \u2192 Model Communication (Direct Function Calls)\n\nThe Controller commands the Model layer through **direct function calls**. This is the primary mechanism for initiating ML operations.\n\n**Example: Training Pipeline (`orchestrator.c:170-257`)**\n```c\n// Controller directly calls Model layer functions:\nif (pipeline_run(tmp_data_dir, preproc_output, sizeof(preproc_output)) != 0) { ... }\n\ntrainer_t *trainer = trainer_factory_create(g_orch.cfg.model_strategy);\ntrainer->train(trainer, preproc_output, &params, &model_info);\n\nif (registry_register_model(&model_info) != 0) { ... }\n```\n\n**Communication Pattern:**\n1. **Synchronous Invocation:** Controller calls Model functions and blocks until completion\n2. **Return Code Propagation:** Model functions return status codes (e.g., `ML_OK`, `ML_ERR_*`)\n3. **Data Passing:** Pointers to configuration structs and output buffers\n\n### 2.3 Model \u2192 Controller Communication (Observer Pattern)\n\nThe Model-to-Controller feedback loop uses the **Observer Pattern** (`observer.h`) to decouple producers from consumers.\n\n**Observer API (`observer.h:119-144`):**\n```c\n// Observable (producer) API\nvoid observable_init(observable_t *observable);\nint observable_subscribe(observable_t *observable, observer_t *subscriber);\nint observable_unsubscribe(observable_t *observable, observer_t *subscriber);\nvoid observable_notify(const observable_t *observable, const observer_event_t *event);\n\n// Event types\ntypedef enum {\n    EVENT_MODEL_DRIFT,\n    EVENT_DATA_DRIFT,\n    EVENT_TRAINING_START,\n    EVENT_TRAINING_END,\n    EVENT_MODEL_VERSION_CREATED,\n    EVENT_ERROR\n} observer_event_type_t;\n```\n\n**Model Monitor Observer Implementation (`model_monitor.c:325-335`):**\n```c\nstatic void notify_observers(ll_model_monitor *mon, const ll_drift_event *event) {\n    pthread_mutex_lock(&mon->lock);\n    for (ll_observer_node *n = mon->observers; n; n = n->next) {\n        n->cb(event, n->user_data);  // Invoke registered callbacks\n    }\n    pthread_mutex_unlock(&mon->lock);\n}\n```\n\n**Communication Pattern:**\n1. **Asynchronous Notification:** Model components emit events without blocking\n2. **Callback Mechanism:** Controller registers callbacks that are invoked on events\n3. **Decoupled Architecture:** Model doesn't need to know what responds to its events\n\n### 2.4 Controller \u2192 View Communication (Push Updates)\n\nThe Controller updates the View layer by **pushing data** through the Dashboard Server's publish API.\n\n**From `orchestrator.c:246-252`:**\n```c\n// After training completes, notify observers (which includes View components)\nobserver_event_t ev = {\n    .type      = OBSERVER_EVT_MODEL_VERSIONED,\n    .timestamp = time(NULL),\n    .payload   = &model_info\n};\nobserver_broadcast(&ev);\n```\n\n**Dashboard Server Publish API (`dashboard_server.h:146-155`):**\n```c\n// Publish JSON to named channel - all subscribed WebSocket clients receive it\ndb_err_t dashboard_server_publish(DashboardServer *srv, const char *channel_name,\n                                   const char *json_payload);\n\n// Broadcast binary data to all clients\ndb_err_t dashboard_server_broadcast(DashboardServer *srv, const void *data,\n                                     size_t data_len, const char *mime_type);\n```\n\n### 2.5 View \u2192 Controller Communication (REST Callbacks)\n\nThe View can trigger Controller actions through **registered HTTP route handlers**.\n\n**From `dashboard_server.h:129-144`:**\n```c\n// Controller registers routes at startup\ndb_err_t dashboard_server_register_route(DashboardServer *srv, const char *method,\n                                         const char *route, dashboard_route_cb cb,\n                                         void *user_ctx);\n\n// Example: Controller registers a retrain endpoint\n// dashboard_server_register_route(srv, \"POST\", \"/api/retrain\", retrain_handler, ctx);\n```\n\n### 2.6 Summary: Communication Mechanisms\n\n| Direction | Mechanism | Example |\n|-----------|-----------|---------|\n| **Controller \u2192 Model** | Direct function calls (synchronous) | `trainer->train()`, `registry_register_model()` |\n| **Model \u2192 Controller** | Observer Pattern callbacks (asynchronous) | `notify_observers()`, `observable_notify()` |\n| **Controller \u2192 View** | Push via publish/broadcast API | `dashboard_server_publish()` |\n| **View \u2192 Controller** | HTTP route callbacks | `/api/retrain` handler |\n\n---\n\n## 3. Critical Workflow Trace: Drift-Triggered Retraining\n\nThis section traces the complete sequence of events when the `DriftDetector` identifies significant data drift, triggering automated retraining.\n\n### 3.1 Workflow Diagram\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510   (1) update() job_factory_create \u2502 LL_JOB_RETRAIN_MODEL\n                                             \u25bc\n Execute job    \u2502 worker thread picks up\n                                             \u25bc\n                   \u2502  (runs Model)   \u2502\n                                    \u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n```\n\n### 3.2 Step-by-Step Trace\n\n#### Step 1: Drift Detection in DriftDetector (`drift_detector.h:314-379`)\n\nThe `DriftDetector` component continuously receives probability distributions from the runtime feature stream. When `lexi_drift_update()` is called:\n\n```c\nvoid lexi_drift_update(lexi_drift_detector_t* det, const double* probs, lexi_error_t* err)\n{\n    // Compute drift metric (PSI, KL divergence, or Wasserstein)\n    switch (det->cfg.metric) {\n        case LEXI_DRIFT_PSI:\n            det->last_score = lexi_compute_psi(det->reference, det->rolling_actual, k);\n            break;\n        // ... other metrics\n    }\n\n    // Check if threshold exceeded\n    bool drift_now = det->last_score >= det->cfg.threshold;\n    if (drift_now && !det->drifting) {\n        det->drifting = true;\n        lexi_notify(det);  // \u2192 Step 2: Fire observer callbacks\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Files:** `src/controller/monitoring/drift_detector.h:314-379`\n\n#### Step 2: DriftDetector Notifies Listeners (`drift_detector.h:257-271`)\n\nThe `lexi_notify()` function invokes all registered listener callbacks:\n\n```c\nstatic void lexi_notify(const lexi_drift_detector_t* det)\n{\n    lexi_drift_event_t evt;\n    strncpy(evt.model_id, det->cfg.model_id, LEXI_MODEL_ID_LEN);\n    evt.score     = det->last_score;\n    evt.threshold = det->cfg.threshold;\n    evt.timestamp = time(NULL);\n\n    for (size_t i = 0; i < det->listener_cnt; ++i) {\n        det->listeners[i](&evt, det->listener_ctx[i]);  // Callback invocation\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Files:** `src/controller/monitoring/drift_detector.h:257-271`\n\n#### Step 3: ModelMonitor Receives Drift Event and Notifies Observers (`model_monitor.c:199-233`)\n\nThe `ModelMonitor` wraps the `DriftDetector` and uses the Observer Pattern to propagate drift events:\n\n```c\nstatic void *monitor_loop(void *arg)\n{\n    while (mon->running) {\n        // ... acquire live metrics\n\n        if (drift_detected(mon, live_acc, live_loss)) {\n            ll_drift_event ev = {\n                .model_id         = mon->model_id,\n                .live_accuracy    = live_acc,\n                .baseline_accuracy= mon->baseline_accuracy,\n                // ...\n            };\n\n            ll_log_warn(\"[Monitor:%s] DRIFT detected\", mon->model_id);\n            notify_observers(mon, &ev);  // \u2192 Step 4\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Files:** `src/controller/monitoring/model_monitor.c:191-233`, `model_monitor.h:79-94`\n\n#### Step 4: RetrainingTrigger Evaluates and Decides (`retraining_trigger.h:368-400`)\n\nThe `RetrainingTrigger` component is registered as an observer. When drift is detected, it evaluates whether retraining is warranted:\n\n```c\nvoid rt_check_and_schedule(void)\n{\n    for (size_t i = 0; i < RT_MAX_MODELS; ++i) {\n        rt_model_entry_t *ent = &_rt_state.entries[i];\n        if (!ent->in_use || ent->retrain_pending) continue;\n\n        if (_rt_drift_detected(ent)) {\n            ent->retrain_pending = true;\n\n            // Invoke registered callback (typically Orchestrator's handler)\n            bool ok = _rt_state.callback(ent->model_id);  // \u2192 Step 5\n\n            if (ok) {\n                ent->count = 0;  // Reset samples for new baseline\n                ent->retrain_pending = false;\n            }\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Files:** `src/controller/monitoring/retraining_trigger.h:368-400`\n\n#### Step 5: Orchestrator Receives Retraining Request (`orchestrator.c:286-303`)\n\nThe `scheduler_mainloop()` in the Orchestrator responds to drift alerts:\n\n```c\nstatic void *scheduler_mainloop(void *arg)\n{\n    while (1) {\n        // Wait for drift alert OR time-based trigger\n        scheduler_wait_or_timeout(interval_hours * 3600);\n\n        // Check for pending drift events\n        if (observer_drift_detected()) {\n            LL_LOG_INFO(ORCHESTRATOR_TAG,\n                        \"Model drift detected \u2013 initiating immediate retraining.\");\n        }\n\n        // Trigger the training pipeline \u2192 Step 6\n        if (start_training_pipeline() != 0) {\n            LL_LOG_ERROR(ORCHESTRATOR_TAG, \"Scheduled training failed\");\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Files:** `src/controller/orchestrator.c:266-307`\n\n#### Step 6: PipelineManager Constructs Training Pipeline (`pipeline_manager.h:203-209`)\n\nThe Orchestrator delegates to the `PipelineManager` to construct the pipeline:\n\n```c\n// From pipeline_manager.h - manual retrain trigger\nint ll_pipeline_manager_trigger_retrain(ll_pipeline_manager_t *mgr);\n```\n\nInternally, this transitions the pipeline through states:\n- `LL_PIPELINE_STATE_INGESTING` \u2192 Data ingestion\n- `LL_PIPELINE_STATE_TRAINING` \u2192 Model training\n- `LL_PIPELINE_STATE_EVALUATING` \u2192 Model evaluation\n- `LL_PIPELINE_STATE_DEPLOYING` \u2192 Deployment (if configured)\n\n**Files:** `src/controller/pipeline/pipeline_manager.h:48-62`, `203-209`\n\n#### Step 7: JobFactory Creates Retraining Job (`job_factory.h:46-55`, `108-111`)\n\nThe `PipelineManager` uses the `JobFactory` to create a retraining job:\n\n```c\ntypedef enum {\n    LL_JOB_TRAIN_MODEL = 0,\n    LL_JOB_HYPERPARAM_TUNE,\n    LL_JOB_RETRAIN_MODEL,     // \u2190 Used for drift-triggered retraining\n    LL_JOB_DATA_PREPROCESS,\n    LL_JOB_MODEL_MONITOR,\n    LL_JOB_MODEL_VERSION_ROLLOUT,\n} ll_job_kind_e;\n\nll_job_status_e job_factory_create(ll_job_kind_e kind, const void *payload_src,\n                                    ll_job_t **job_out);\n```\n\nThe job encapsulates:\n- `job_id`: Unique identifier\n- `submitted_by`: Audit trail\n- `kind`: `LL_JOB_RETRAIN_MODEL`\n- `payload`: Model-specific configuration\n\n**Files:** `src/controller/job_factory/job_factory.h:46-55`, `108-111`\n\n#### Step 8: TaskScheduler Executes the Job (`task_scheduler.h:173-182`)\n\nThe created job is handed to the `TaskScheduler` for execution:\n\n```c\nint lxl_task_scheduler_schedule_once(lxl_task_scheduler_t *scheduler,\n                                      const char *task_id,\n                                      const char *task_name,\n                                      lxl_task_fn_t cb,        // Training callback\n                                      void *user_ctx,          // Job context\n                                      time_t run_at,           // 0 = immediate\n                                      int priority);           // Higher = sooner\n```\n\nThe scheduler:\n1. Adds the job to its priority queue\n2. A worker thread picks up the job\n3. Executes the training callback\n4. Emits `LXL_SCHED_EVENT_TASK_SUCCESS` or `LXL_SCHED_EVENT_TASK_FAILURE`\n\n**Files:** `src/controller/scheduler/task_scheduler.h:156-206`\n\n### 3.3 Event Flow Summary\n\n| Step | Component | File | Action |\n|------|-----------|------|--------|\n| 1 | DriftDetector | `drift_detector.h:314-379` | Computes drift score, detects threshold breach |\n| 2 | DriftDetector | `drift_detector.h:257-271` | Fires `lexi_notify()` to listeners |\n| 3 | ModelMonitor | `model_monitor.c:191-233` | Aggregates monitoring, calls `notify_observers()` |\n| 4 | RetrainingTrigger | `retraining_trigger.h:368-400` | Evaluates drift, invokes callback to Orchestrator |\n| 5 | Orchestrator | `orchestrator.c:266-307` | Receives alert, initiates `start_training_pipeline()` |\n| 6 | PipelineManager | `pipeline_manager.h:203-209` | Orchestrates pipeline stages |\n| 7 | JobFactory | `job_factory.h:108-111` | Creates `LL_JOB_RETRAIN_MODEL` job |\n| 8 | TaskScheduler | `task_scheduler.h:173-206` | Schedules and executes job on worker thread |\n\n---\n\n## 4. Architectural Critique\n\n### 4.1 Benefits of MVC in This Context\n\n#### 4.1.1 Clear Separation of Concerns\n\n**Evidence:** The directory structure enforces strict boundaries:\n- `src/model/` contains ~30% of the codebase and zero orchestration logic\n- `src/controller/` contains ~50% and zero ML algorithms\n- `src/view/` contains ~20% and purely presentation code\n\n**Impact:** Teams can work independently:\n- ML engineers modify `model_strategy.h` implementations without touching the Controller\n- DevOps engineers modify `task_scheduler.h` without understanding NLP\n- Frontend engineers modify `dashboard_server.h` without ML knowledge\n\n#### 4.1.2 Strategy Pattern Enables Hot-Swapping\n\n**Evidence (`model_strategy.h:194-203`):**\n```c\nlexi_status_t ll_strategy_register(const char *name, strategy_ctor_fn ctor);\nmodel_strategy_t *ll_strategy_create(const char *name);\n```\n\n**Impact:** Educators can swap algorithms at runtime:\n- Change `orchestrator.toml: active = \"lexi_summarizer\"` \u2192 no recompilation\n- Add new strategy by implementing vtable \u2192 Controller unchanged\n\n#### 4.1.3 Observer Pattern Decouples Monitoring\n\n**Evidence (`observer.h:120-144`):**\n- `observable_subscribe()` and `observable_notify()` allow loose coupling\n- DriftDetector doesn't need to know about RetrainingTrigger\n\n**Impact:**\n- Adding new observers (e.g., Slack alerter) requires zero changes to Model or existing observers\n- Testing becomes easier\u2014mock observers can verify event emission\n\n#### 4.1.4 Modular, Testable Architecture\n\n**Evidence:**\n- Each component has a clean public API (headers in `include/lexilearn/`)\n- Components can be unit-tested in isolation\n- CI enforces \u226585% code coverage\n\n**Impact:** Maintainability over time\u2014new developers can understand and modify components without deep system knowledge.\n\n### 4.2 Drawbacks and Architectural Smells\n\n#### 4.2.1 MVC is Designed for User Interaction Loops, Not Event-Driven Backend Processes\n\n**Problem:** MVC was conceived for GUI applications with tight request-response cycles:\n- User action \u2192 Controller \u2192 Model update \u2192 View refresh\n\n**Evidence in LexiLearn:**\n- The \"request\" is not a user click but a cron timer or drift threshold\n- The \"response\" is not a GUI update but a multi-hour training job\n- The View (`dashboard_server.h`) is not a GUI but a data server\n\n**Impact:** The metaphor is stretched:\n- \"View\" is really a \"Notifier/Reporter\"\n- \"Controller\" is really an \"Orchestrator/Scheduler\"\n- Developers familiar with MVC may have incorrect mental models\n\n#### 4.2.2 Bloated Controller Layer\n\n**Problem:** The Controller has accumulated too many responsibilities.\n\n**Evidence:**\n- `src/controller/` contains: orchestrator, pipeline, job_factory, monitoring, scheduler\n- The `orchestrator.c` alone handles: initialization, training pipelines, signal handling, observer notifications\n\n**Metrics:**\n- Controller: ~15 source files, ~50% of codebase\n- Model: ~12 source files, ~30% of codebase\n- View: ~3 source files, ~10% of codebase\n\n**Impact:**\n- Testing the Controller requires mocking many dependencies\n- Changes to scheduling logic risk breaking training logic\n- Violates Single Responsibility Principle\n\n#### 4.2.3 Awkward Model-to-Controller Communication in C\n\n**Problem:** Traditional MVC frameworks provide elegant data binding (e.g., iOS KVO, Android LiveData). C lacks these abstractions.\n\n**Evidence:** The Observer Pattern implementation (`observer.h`) is manual:\n```c\ntypedef struct {\n    observer_t *subscribers[OBSERVER_MAX_SUBSCRIBERS];  // Fixed-size array\n    size_t count;\n} observable_t;\n```\n\n**Impact:**\n- `OBSERVER_MAX_SUBSCRIBERS = 32` is a hard limit requiring recompilation to change\n- No type safety\u2014`void *payload` requires careful casting\n- Memory management is manual (caller must not free static strings)\n- Thread-safety is bolt-on (`pthread_mutex_t` in each component)\n\n#### 4.2.4 Singleton Anti-Pattern in Orchestrator\n\n**Problem:** The Orchestrator uses a global singleton (`orchestrator.c:53-57`):\n```c\nstatic orchestrator_t g_orch = {\n    .initialized = 0,\n    .running     = 0,\n    .state_mtx   = PTHREAD_MUTEX_INITIALIZER\n};\n```\n\n**Impact:**\n- Only one Orchestrator per process (can't run isolated test instances)\n- Global state complicates unit testing\n- Initialization order dependencies\n\n#### 4.2.5 View Layer is Non-Standard\n\n**Problem:** The \"View\" is a WebSocket/HTTP server, not a UI.\n\n**Evidence (`dashboard_server.h`):**\n- Publishes JSON to channels\n- Broadcasts binary blobs (heat-maps)\n- No user-facing UI rendering\n\n**Impact:**\n- The MVC terminology is misleading\n- Would be more accurately called \"Reporter\" or \"Gateway\"\n- New developers may expect rendering logic\n\n#### 4.2.6 Tight Coupling Despite Observer Pattern\n\n**Problem:** Despite using Observer Pattern, there's implicit coupling through shared data structures.\n\n**Evidence:**\n- `observer_event_t` is defined in Controller but used by Model components\n- `mm_metrics_t` (Model Monitor metrics) is shared across layers\n- Error codes are inconsistent (`ll_status_t`, `mm_status_t`, `ml_error_t`, `db_err_t`)\n\n**Impact:**\n- Changes to event structures require coordinated updates\n- No interface versioning\u2014breaking changes propagate immediately\n\n#### 4.2.7 Missing CQRS for ML Workloads\n\n**Problem:** ML systems typically benefit from Command-Query Responsibility Segregation (CQRS):\n- **Commands:** Train model, trigger retraining (long-running, async)\n- **Queries:** Get model metrics, list experiments (fast, sync)\n\n**Evidence:** LexiLearn conflates both:\n- `orchestrator.c` handles both commands (`start_training_pipeline()`) and queries (`registry_register_model()`)\n- No separate read models for dashboard queries\n\n**Impact:**\n- Dashboard queries may contend with training locks\n- Scaling read vs. write paths requires significant refactoring\n\n### 4.3 Recommendations\n\n1. **Rename Layers to Match Domain:**\n   - \"Controller\" \u2192 \"Orchestrator\" or \"Coordinator\"\n   - \"View\" \u2192 \"Gateway\" or \"Reporter\"\n   - \"Model\" \u2192 \"Core\" or \"Engine\"\n\n2. **Extract Sub-Orchestrators:**\n   - Move scheduling to a dedicated `SchedulingService`\n   - Move monitoring to a dedicated `MonitoringService`\n   - Keep `Orchestrator` as a thin coordinator\n\n3. **Introduce Event Bus:**\n   - Replace ad-hoc Observer Pattern with a centralized event bus\n   - Add event versioning for backwards compatibility\n\n4. **Adopt CQRS:**\n   - Separate write path (training, registration) from read path (dashboards, queries)\n   - Use eventual consistency for dashboard data\n\n5. **Remove Singleton:**\n   - Pass Orchestrator instance via dependency injection\n   - Enables isolated testing and multi-tenant scenarios\n\n---\n\n## 5. Conclusion\n\nThe LexiLearn MVC Orchestrator demonstrates a thoughtful application of the MVC pattern to an ML orchestration domain. The architecture provides clear separation of concerns, enables hot-swapping of ML strategies, and uses the Observer Pattern for loose coupling.\n\nHowever, the MVC metaphor is stretched in this context. The \"View\" is a data server, not a UI. The \"Controller\" has accumulated too many responsibilities. The manual Observer Pattern implementation in C lacks the elegance of framework-provided bindings.\n\nFor new team members, the key insights are:\n1. **Model = ML Logic + Data Persistence** \u2014 treat it as a library you call\n2. **Controller = Orchestration + Monitoring + Scheduling** \u2014 this is where decisions happen\n3. **View = External Communication** \u2014 REST/WebSocket gateway to dashboards\n4. **Communication = Function calls down, callbacks up**\n\nThe architecture is production-ready and has clearly been designed with MLOps principles in mind. Future improvements should focus on reducing Controller complexity and adopting patterns more native to event-driven backend systems.\n\n---\n\n## Appendix A: Key File References\n\n| Component | Header | Implementation |\n|-----------|--------|----------------|\n| Orchestrator | `src/controller/orchestrator.h` | `src/controller/orchestrator.c` |\n| Pipeline Manager | `src/controller/pipeline/pipeline_manager.h` | (impl in .c) |\n| Drift Detector | `src/controller/monitoring/drift_detector.h` | (header-only) |\n| Model Monitor | `src/controller/monitoring/model_monitor.h` | `src/controller/monitoring/model_monitor.c` |\n| Retraining Trigger | `src/controller/monitoring/retraining_trigger.h` | (header-only) |\n| Observer | `src/controller/monitoring/observer.h` | (header-only) |\n| Job Factory | `src/controller/job_factory/job_factory.h` | (impl in .c) |\n| Task Scheduler | `src/controller/scheduler/task_scheduler.h` | (impl in .c) |\n| Model Registry | `src/model/ml_pipeline/model_registry.h` | (impl in .c) |\n| Model Strategy | `src/model/ml_models/model_strategy.h` | (impl by concrete strategies) |\n| Dashboard Server | `src/view/dashboard_server.h` | (impl in .c) |\n\n## Appendix B: Design Pattern Summary\n\n| Pattern | Location | Purpose |\n|---------|----------|---------|\n| **MVC** | Entire architecture | Separation of concerns |\n| **Strategy** | `model_strategy.h` | Hot-swappable ML algorithms |\n| **Factory** | `job_factory.h` | Create diverse job types |\n| **Observer** | `observer.h` | Decouple event producers/consumers |\n| **Pipeline** | `pipeline_manager.h` | Orchestrate ETL \u2192 Train \u2192 Deploy |\n| **Singleton** | `orchestrator.c` | Global orchestrator instance (anti-pattern) |\n",

  "content": "# LexiLearn MVC Orchestrator: Architectural Analysis and Critique\n\n**Document Type:** Onboarding Guide for Senior Developers\n**Version:** 1.0\n**Author:** Architecture Team\n**Date:** 2024\n\n---\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nThis document provides a definitive guide to the LexiLearn MVC Orchestrator's architecture, a C-based system for managing NLP/ML model pipelines with automated retraining, monitoring, and versioning. The system unconventionally applies the Model-View-Controller (MVC) pattern to an ML orchestration domain. This guide maps the components to MVC roles, describes communication pathways, traces a critical workflow, and provides a balanced architectural critique.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Component Mapping to MVC Roles\n\nThe LexiLearn Orchestrator implements a clear MVC pattern through its directory structure and component responsibilities. Below is the mapping with justifications:\n\n### 1.1 Model Layer (`src/model/`)\n\nThe **Model** layer encapsulates all machine learning and data-related logic. It is completely agnostic to orchestration concerns and can operate independently.\n\n| Directory/Component | File(s) | Purpose & Role |\n|---------------------|---------|----------------|\n| **Preprocessing** | `text_cleaner.{c,h}`, `tokenizer.{c,h}` | Text normalization and tokenization (BPE, WordPiece, SentencePiece) |\n| **ML Models** | `model_strategy.h`, `transformer_summarizer.{c,h}`, `ngram_analyzer.{c,h}`, `hybrid_model.{c,h}` | Strategy Pattern implementations for pluggable algorithms |\n| **ML Pipeline** | `model_trainer.{c,h}`, `model_evaluator.{c,h}`, `experiment_tracker.{c,h}` | Training orchestration, metrics computation, experiment tracking |\n| **Model Registry** | `model_registry.{c,h}` | SQLite-backed versioning, lifecycle management (EXPERIMENT \u2192 STAGING \u2192 PRODUCTION \u2192 ARCHIVED), model lineage |\n| **Feature Store** | `feature_store_manager.{c,h}` | Versioned feature storage and retrieval |\n\n**Justification:** The Model layer contains:\n- All domain-specific ML logic (training, inference, evaluation)\n- Data persistence (Model Registry)\n- No knowledge of scheduling, monitoring, or presentation concerns\n- Pure business logic that could theoretically be extracted into a library\n\nThe `model_strategy.h` file (`src/model/ml_models/model_strategy.h:96-173`) defines the Strategy Pattern vtable:\n\n```c\ntypedef struct model_strategy_vtable {\n    lexi_status_t (*configure)(model_strategy_t *self, const hyperparam_t *params, size_t param_count);\n    lexi_status_t (*train)(model_strategy_t *self, const ll_dataset_t *training_data, ...);\n    lexi_status_t (*predict)(model_strategy_t *self, const ll_dataset_t *input_data, ...);\n    lexi_status_t (*evaluate)(model_strategy_t *self, const ll_dataset_t *test_data, double *out_score);\n    lexi_status_t (*save)(model_strategy_t *self, const char *artifact_uri);\n    lexi_status_t (*load)(model_strategy_t *self, const char *artifact_uri);\n    void (*destroy)(model_strategy_t *self);\n} model_strategy_vtable_t;\n```\n\n### 1.2 View Layer (`src/view/`)\n\nThe **View** layer handles all presentation and external communication concerns.\n\n| Component | File(s) | Purpose & Role |\n|-----------|---------|----------------|\n| **Dashboard Server** | `dashboard_server.{c,h}` | HTTP/WebSocket server for real-time dashboards, metrics streaming, educator control panels |\n\n**Justification:** The View layer:\n- Exposes REST endpoints (e.g., `/api/retrain`) for manual interventions\n- Provides WebSocket channels for real-time metric push to dashboards\n- Handles TLS/HTTPS, CORS, and client connection management\n- Contains no ML logic\u2014purely concerned with presenting data and accepting user commands\n\nFrom `dashboard_server.h:85-91`:\n```c\ntypedef int (*dashboard_route_cb)(\n    const char *uri,\n    const char *request_body,\n    size_t request_len,\n    char **response_body,\n    size_t *response_len,\n    void *user_ctx);\n```\n\n### 1.3 Controller Layer (`src/controller/`)\n\nThe **Controller** layer orchestrates the entire system, mediating between Model and View.\n\n| Directory/Component | File(s) | Purpose & Role |\n|---------------------|---------|----------------|\n| **Orchestrator** | `orchestrator.{c,h}` | Central command center coordinating the entire MLOps pipeline |\n| **Pipeline** | `pipeline_manager.{c,h}`, `ingestion_stage.{c,h}`, `training_stage.{c,h}`, `deployment_stage.{c,h}` | Pipeline Pattern for ETL \u2192 Training \u2192 Deployment |\n| **Job Factory** | `job_factory.{c,h}`, `job_types.h` | Factory Pattern for creating diverse training jobs |\n| **Monitoring** | `model_monitor.{c,h}`, `drift_detector.{c,h}`, `observer.h`, `retraining_trigger.{c,h}` | Drift detection, Observer Pattern for events, automated retraining triggers |\n| **Scheduler** | `task_scheduler.{c,h}` | Cron-like scheduling for automated tasks |\n\n**Justification:** The Controller layer:\n- Coordinates workflow between Model and View\n- Makes decisions about when to retrain, what strategy to use\n- Contains no ML algorithms\u2014delegates to Model layer\n- Contains no presentation logic\u2014delegates to View layer\n- Implements the Observer Pattern to decouple drift detection from retraining\n\nFrom `orchestrator.c:165-257`, the `start_training_pipeline()` function shows the Controller coordinating Model components:\n```c\n// 1. Ingest \u2192 2. Preprocess \u2192 3. Hyperparameter Tuning \u2192 4. Train via Factory \u2192 5. Register \u2192 6. Notify\n```\n\n---\n\n## 2. Communication Pathways and Data Flow\n\n### 2.1 High-Level Communication Architecture\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502 \u2502\n\u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n```\n\n### 2.2 Controller \u2192 Model Communication (Direct Function Calls)\n\nThe Controller commands the Model layer through **direct function calls**. This is the primary mechanism for initiating ML operations.\n\n**Example: Training Pipeline (`orchestrator.c:170-257`)**\n```c\n// Controller directly calls Model layer functions:\nif (pipeline_run(tmp_data_dir, preproc_output, sizeof(preproc_output)) != 0) { ... }\n\ntrainer_t *trainer = trainer_factory_create(g_orch.cfg.model_strategy);\ntrainer->train(trainer, preproc_output, &params, &model_info);\n\nif (registry_register_model(&model_info) != 0) { ... }\n```\n\n**Communication Pattern:**\n1. **Synchronous Invocation:** Controller calls Model functions and blocks until completion\n2. **Return Code Propagation:** Model functions return status codes (e.g., `ML_OK`, `ML_ERR_*`)\n3. **Data Passing:** Pointers to configuration structs and output buffers\n\n### 2.3 Model \u2192 Controller Communication (Observer Pattern)\n\nThe Model-to-Controller feedback loop uses the **Observer Pattern** (`observer.h`) to decouple producers from consumers.\n\n**Observer API (`observer.h:119-144`):**\n```c\n// Observable (producer) API\nvoid observable_init(observable_t *observable);\nint observable_subscribe(observable_t *observable, observer_t *subscriber);\nint observable_unsubscribe(observable_t *observable, observer_t *subscriber);\nvoid observable_notify(const observable_t *observable, const observer_event_t *event);\n\n// Event types\ntypedef enum {\n    EVENT_MODEL_DRIFT,\n    EVENT_DATA_DRIFT,\n    EVENT_TRAINING_START,\n    EVENT_TRAINING_END,\n    EVENT_MODEL_VERSION_CREATED,\n    EVENT_ERROR\n} observer_event_type_t;\n```\n\n**Model Monitor Observer Implementation (`model_monitor.c:325-335`):**\n```c\nstatic void notify_observers(ll_model_monitor *mon, const ll_drift_event *event) {\n    pthread_mutex_lock(&mon->lock);\n    for (ll_observer_node *n = mon->observers; n; n = n->next) {\n        n->cb(event, n->user_data);  // Invoke registered callbacks\n    }\n    pthread_mutex_unlock(&mon->lock);\n}\n```\n\n**Communication Pattern:**\n1. **Asynchronous Notification:** Model components emit events without blocking\n2. **Callback Mechanism:** Controller registers callbacks that are invoked on events\n3. **Decoupled Architecture:** Model doesn't need to know what responds to its events\n\n### 2.4 Controller \u2192 View Communication (Push Updates)\n\nThe Controller updates the View layer by **pushing data** through the Dashboard Server's publish API.\n\n**From `orchestrator.c:246-252`:**\n```c\n// After training completes, notify observers (which includes View components)\nobserver_event_t ev = {\n    .type      = OBSERVER_EVT_MODEL_VERSIONED,\n    .timestamp = time(NULL),\n    .payload   = &model_info\n};\nobserver_broadcast(&ev);\n```\n\n**Dashboard Server Publish API (`dashboard_server.h:146-155`):**\n```c\n// Publish JSON to named channel - all subscribed WebSocket clients receive it\ndb_err_t dashboard_server_publish(DashboardServer *srv, const char *channel_name,\n                                   const char *json_payload);\n\n// Broadcast binary data to all clients\ndb_err_t dashboard_server_broadcast(DashboardServer *srv, const void *data,\n                                     size_t data_len, const char *mime_type);\n```\n\n### 2.5 View \u2192 Controller Communication (REST Callbacks)\n\nThe View can trigger Controller actions through **registered HTTP route handlers**.\n\n**From `dashboard_server.h:129-144`:**\n```c\n// Controller registers routes at startup\ndb_err_t dashboard_server_register_route(DashboardServer *srv, const char *method,\n                                         const char *route, dashboard_route_cb cb,\n                                         void *user_ctx);\n\n// Example: Controller registers a retrain endpoint\n// dashboard_server_register_route(srv, \"POST\", \"/api/retrain\", retrain_handler, ctx);\n```\n\n### 2.6 Summary: Communication Mechanisms\n\n| Direction | Mechanism | Example |\n|-----------|-----------|---------|\n| **Controller \u2192 Model** | Direct function calls (synchronous) | `trainer->train()`, `registry_register_model()` |\n| **Model \u2192 Controller** | Observer Pattern callbacks (asynchronous) | `notify_observers()`, `observable_notify()` |\n| **Controller \u2192 View** | Push via publish/broadcast API | `dashboard_server_publish()` |\n| **View \u2192 Controller** | HTTP route callbacks | `/api/retrain` handler |\n\n---\n\n## 3. Critical Workflow Trace: Drift-Triggered Retraining\n\nThis section traces the complete sequence of events when the `DriftDetector` identifies significant data drift, triggering automated retraining.\n\n### 3.1 Workflow Diagram\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510   (1) update() (`drift_detector.h:314-379`)\n\nThe `DriftDetector` component continuously receives probability distributions from the runtime feature stream. When `lexi_drift_update()` is called:\n\n```c\nvoid lexi_drift_update(lexi_drift_detector_t* det, const double* probs, lexi_error_t* err)\n{\n    // Compute drift metric (PSI, KL divergence, or Wasserstein)\n    switch (det->cfg.metric) {\n        case LEXI_DRIFT_PSI:\n            det->last_score = lexi_compute_psi(det->reference, det->rolling_actual, k);\n            break;\n        // ... other metrics\n    }\n\n    // Check if threshold exceeded\n    bool drift_now = det->last_score >= det->cfg.threshold;\n    if (drift_now && !det->drifting) {\n        det->drifting = true;\n        lexi_notify(det);  // \u2192 Step 2: Fire observer callbacks\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Files:** `src/controller/monitoring/drift_detector.h:314-379`\n\n#### Step 2: DriftDetector Notifies Listeners (`drift_detector.h:257-271`)\n\nThe `lexi_notify()` function invokes all registered listener callbacks:\n\n```c\nstatic void lexi_notify(const lexi_drift_detector_t* det)\n{\n    lexi_drift_event_t evt;\n    strncpy(evt.model_id, det->cfg.model_id, LEXI_MODEL_ID_LEN);\n    evt.score     = det->last_score;\n    evt.threshold = det->cfg.threshold;\n    evt.timestamp = time(NULL);\n\n    for (size_t i = 0; i < det->listener_cnt; ++i) {\n        det->listeners[i](&evt, det->listener_ctx[i]);  // Callback invocation\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Files:** `src/controller/monitoring/drift_detector.h:257-271`\n\n#### Step 3: ModelMonitor Receives Drift Event and Notifies Observers (`model_monitor.c:199-233`)\n\nThe `ModelMonitor` wraps the `DriftDetector` and uses the Observer Pattern to propagate drift events:\n\n```c\nstatic void *monitor_loop(void *arg)\n{\n    while (mon->running) {\n        // ... acquire live metrics\n\n        if (drift_detected(mon, live_acc, live_loss)) {\n            ll_drift_event ev = {\n                .model_id         = mon->model_id,\n                .live_accuracy    = live_acc,\n                .baseline_accuracy= mon->baseline_accuracy,\n                // ...\n            };\n\n            ll_log_warn(\"[Monitor:%s] DRIFT detected\", mon->model_id);\n            notify_observers(mon, &ev);  // \u2192 Step 4\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Files:** `src/controller/monitoring/model_monitor.c:191-233`, `model_monitor.h:79-94`\n\n#### Step 4: RetrainingTrigger Evaluates and Decides (`retraining_trigger.h:368-400`)\n\nThe `RetrainingTrigger` component is registered as an observer. When drift is detected, it evaluates whether retraining is warranted:\n\n```c\nvoid rt_check_and_schedule(void)\n{\n    for (size_t i = 0; i < RT_MAX_MODELS; ++i) {\n        rt_model_entry_t *ent = &_rt_state.entries[i];\n        if (!ent->in_use || ent->retrain_pending) continue;\n\n        if (_rt_drift_detected(ent)) {\n            ent->retrain_pending = true;\n\n            // Invoke registered callback (typically Orchestrator's handler)\n            bool ok = _rt_state.callback(ent->model_id);  // \u2192 Step 5\n\n            if (ok) {\n                ent->count = 0;  // Reset samples for new baseline\n                ent->retrain_pending = false;\n            }\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Files:** `src/controller/monitoring/retraining_trigger.h:368-400`\n\n#### Step 5: Orchestrator Receives Retraining Request (`orchestrator.c:286-303`)\n\nThe `scheduler_mainloop()` in the Orchestrator responds to drift alerts:\n\n```c\nstatic void *scheduler_mainloop(void *arg)\n{\n    while (1) {\n        // Wait for drift alert OR time-based trigger\n        scheduler_wait_or_timeout(interval_hours * 3600);\n\n        // Check for pending drift events\n        if (observer_drift_detected()) {\n            LL_LOG_INFO(ORCHESTRATOR_TAG,\n                        \"Model drift detected \u2013 initiating immediate retraining.\");\n        }\n\n        // Trigger the training pipeline \u2192 Step 6\n        if (start_training_pipeline() != 0) {\n            LL_LOG_ERROR(ORCHESTRATOR_TAG, \"Scheduled training failed\");\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Files:** `src/controller/orchestrator.c:266-307`\n\n#### Step 6: PipelineManager Constructs Training Pipeline (`pipeline_manager.h:203-209`)\n\nThe Orchestrator delegates to the `PipelineManager` to construct the pipeline:\n\n```c\n// From pipeline_manager.h - manual retrain trigger\nint ll_pipeline_manager_trigger_retrain(ll_pipeline_manager_t *mgr);\n```\n\nInternally, this transitions the pipeline through states:\n- `LL_PIPELINE_STATE_INGESTING` \u2192 Data ingestion\n- `LL_PIPELINE_STATE_TRAINING` \u2192 Model training\n- `LL_PIPELINE_STATE_EVALUATING` \u2192 Model evaluation\n- `LL_PIPELINE_STATE_DEPLOYING` \u2192 Deployment (if configured)\n\n**Files:** `src/controller/pipeline/pipeline_manager.h:48-62`, `203-209`\n\n#### Step 7: JobFactory Creates Retraining Job (`job_factory.h:46-55`, `108-111`)\n\nThe `PipelineManager` uses the `JobFactory` to create a retraining job:\n\n```c\ntypedef enum {\n    LL_JOB_TRAIN_MODEL = 0,\n    LL_JOB_HYPERPARAM_TUNE,\n    LL_JOB_RETRAIN_MODEL,     // \u2190 Used for drift-triggered retraining\n    LL_JOB_DATA_PREPROCESS,\n    LL_JOB_MODEL_MONITOR,\n    LL_JOB_MODEL_VERSION_ROLLOUT,\n} ll_job_kind_e;\n\nll_job_status_e job_factory_create(ll_job_kind_e kind, const void *payload_src,\n                                    ll_job_t **job_out);\n```\n\nThe job encapsulates:\n- `job_id`: Unique identifier\n- `submitted_by`: Audit trail\n- `kind`: `LL_JOB_RETRAIN_MODEL`\n- `payload`: Model-specific configuration\n\n**Files:** `src/controller/job_factory/job_factory.h:46-55`, `108-111`\n\n#### Step 8: TaskScheduler Executes the Job (`task_scheduler.h:173-182`)\n\nThe created job is handed to the `TaskScheduler` for execution:\n\n```c\nint lxl_task_scheduler_schedule_once(lxl_task_scheduler_t *scheduler,\n                                      const char *task_id,\n                                      const char *task_name,\n                                      lxl_task_fn_t cb,        // Training callback\n                                      void *user_ctx,          // Job context\n                                      time_t run_at,           // 0 = immediate\n                                      int priority);           // Higher = sooner\n```\n\nThe scheduler:\n1. Adds the job to its priority queue\n2. A worker thread picks up the job\n3. Executes the training callback\n4. Emits `LXL_SCHED_EVENT_TASK_SUCCESS` or `LXL_SCHED_EVENT_TASK_FAILURE`\n\n**Files:** `src/controller/scheduler/task_scheduler.h:156-206`\n\n### 3.3 Event Flow Summary\n\n| Step | Component | File | Action |\n|------|-----------|------|--------|\n| 1 | DriftDetector | `drift_detector.h:314-379` | Computes drift score, detects threshold breach |\n| 2 | DriftDetector | `drift_detector.h:257-271` | Fires `lexi_notify()` to listeners |\n| 3 | ModelMonitor | `model_monitor.c:191-233` | Aggregates monitoring, calls `notify_observers()` |\n| 4 | RetrainingTrigger | `retraining_trigger.h:368-400` | Evaluates drift, invokes callback to Orchestrator |\n| 5 | Orchestrator | `orchestrator.c:266-307` | Receives alert, initiates `start_training_pipeline()` |\n| 6 | PipelineManager | `pipeline_manager.h:203-209` | Orchestrates pipeline stages |\n| 7 | JobFactory | `job_factory.h:108-111` | Creates `LL_JOB_RETRAIN_MODEL` job |\n| 8 | TaskScheduler | `task_scheduler.h:173-206` | Schedules and executes job on worker thread |\n\n---\n\n## 4. Architectural Critique\n\n### 4.1 Benefits of MVC in This Context\n\n#### 4.1.1 Clear Separation of Concerns\n\n**Evidence:** The directory structure enforces strict boundaries:\n- `src/model/` contains ~30% of the codebase and zero orchestration logic\n- `src/controller/` contains ~50% and zero ML algorithms\n- `src/view/` contains ~20% and purely presentation code\n\n**Impact:** Teams can work independently:\n- ML engineers modify `model_strategy.h` implementations without touching the Controller\n- DevOps engineers modify `task_scheduler.h` without understanding NLP\n- Frontend engineers modify `dashboard_server.h` without ML knowledge\n\n#### 4.1.2 Strategy Pattern Enables Hot-Swapping\n\n**Evidence (`model_strategy.h:194-203`):**\n```c\nlexi_status_t ll_strategy_register(const char *name, strategy_ctor_fn ctor);\nmodel_strategy_t *ll_strategy_create(const char *name);\n```\n\n**Impact:** Educators can swap algorithms at runtime:\n- Change `orchestrator.toml: active = \"lexi_summarizer\"` \u2192 no recompilation\n- Add new strategy by implementing vtable \u2192 Controller unchanged\n\n#### 4.1.3 Observer Pattern Decouples Monitoring\n\n**Evidence (`observer.h:120-144`):**\n- `observable_subscribe()` and `observable_notify()` allow loose coupling\n- DriftDetector doesn't need to know about RetrainingTrigger\n\n**Impact:**\n- Adding new observers (e.g., Slack alerter) requires zero changes to Model or existing observers\n- Testing becomes easier\u2014mock observers can verify event emission\n\n#### 4.1.4 Modular, Testable Architecture\n\n**Evidence:**\n- Each component has a clean public API (headers in `include/lexilearn/`)\n- Components can be unit-tested in isolation\n- CI enforces \u226585% code coverage\n\n**Impact:** Maintainability over time\u2014new developers can understand and modify components without deep system knowledge.\n\n### 4.2 Drawbacks and Architectural Smells\n\n#### 4.2.1 MVC is Designed for User Interaction Loops, Not Event-Driven Backend Processes\n\n**Problem:** MVC was conceived for GUI applications with tight request-response cycles:\n- User action \u2192 Controller \u2192 Model update \u2192 View refresh\n\n**Evidence in LexiLearn:**\n- The \"request\" is not a user click but a cron timer or drift threshold\n- The \"response\" is not a GUI update but a multi-hour training job\n- The View (`dashboard_server.h`) is not a GUI but a data server\n\n**Impact:** The metaphor is stretched:\n- \"View\" is really a \"Notifier/Reporter\"\n- \"Controller\" is really an \"Orchestrator/Scheduler\"\n- Developers familiar with MVC may have incorrect mental models\n\n#### 4.2.2 Bloated Controller Layer\n\n**Problem:** The Controller has accumulated too many responsibilities.\n\n**Evidence:**\n- `src/controller/` contains: orchestrator, pipeline, job_factory, monitoring, scheduler\n- The `orchestrator.c` alone handles: initialization, training pipelines, signal handling, observer notifications\n\n**Metrics:**\n- Controller: ~15 source files, ~50% of codebase\n- Model: ~12 source files, ~30% of codebase\n- View: ~3 source files, ~10% of codebase\n\n**Impact:**\n- Testing the Controller requires mocking many dependencies\n- Changes to scheduling logic risk breaking training logic\n- Violates Single Responsibility Principle\n\n#### 4.2.3 Awkward Model-to-Controller Communication in C\n\n**Problem:** Traditional MVC frameworks provide elegant data binding (e.g., iOS KVO, Android LiveData). C lacks these abstractions.\n\n**Evidence:** The Observer Pattern implementation (`observer.h`) is manual:\n```c\ntypedef struct {\n    observer_t *subscribers[OBSERVER_MAX_SUBSCRIBERS];  // Fixed-size array\n    size_t count;\n} observable_t;\n```\n\n**Impact:**\n- `OBSERVER_MAX_SUBSCRIBERS = 32` is a hard limit requiring recompilation to change\n- No type safety\u2014`void *payload` requires careful casting\n- Memory management is manual (caller must not free static strings)\n- Thread-safety is bolt-on (`pthread_mutex_t` in each component)\n\n#### 4.2.4 Singleton Anti-Pattern in Orchestrator\n\n**Problem:** The Orchestrator uses a global singleton (`orchestrator.c:53-57`):\n```c\nstatic orchestrator_t g_orch = {\n    .initialized = 0,\n    .running     = 0,\n    .state_mtx   = PTHREAD_MUTEX_INITIALIZER\n};\n```\n\n**Impact:**\n- Only one Orchestrator per process (can't run isolated test instances)\n- Global state complicates unit testing\n- Initialization order dependencies\n\n#### 4.2.5 View Layer is Non-Standard\n\n**Problem:** The \"View\" is a WebSocket/HTTP server, not a UI.\n\n**Evidence (`dashboard_server.h`):**\n- Publishes JSON to channels\n- Broadcasts binary blobs (heat-maps)\n- No user-facing UI rendering\n\n**Impact:**\n- The MVC terminology is misleading\n- Would be more accurately called \"Reporter\" or \"Gateway\"\n- New developers may expect rendering logic\n\n#### 4.2.6 Tight Coupling Despite Observer Pattern\n\n**Problem:** Despite using Observer Pattern, there's implicit coupling through shared data structures.\n\n**Evidence:**\n- `observer_event_t` is defined in Controller but used by Model components\n- `mm_metrics_t` (Model Monitor metrics) is shared across layers\n- Error codes are inconsistent (`ll_status_t`, `mm_status_t`, `ml_error_t`, `db_err_t`)\n\n**Impact:**\n- Changes to event structures require coordinated updates\n- No interface versioning\u2014breaking changes propagate immediately\n\n#### 4.2.7 Missing CQRS for ML Workloads\n\n**Problem:** ML systems typically benefit from Command-Query Responsibility Segregation (CQRS):\n- **Commands:** Train model, trigger retraining (long-running, async)\n- **Queries:** Get model metrics, list experiments (fast, sync)\n\n**Evidence:** LexiLearn conflates both:\n- `orchestrator.c` handles both commands (`start_training_pipeline()`) and queries (`registry_register_model()`)\n- No separate read models for dashboard queries\n\n**Impact:**\n- Dashboard queries may contend with training locks\n- Scaling read vs. write paths requires significant refactoring\n\n### 4.3 Recommendations\n\n1. **Rename Layers to Match Domain:**\n   - \"Controller\" \u2192 \"Orchestrator\" or \"Coordinator\"\n   - \"View\" \u2192 \"Gateway\" or \"Reporter\"\n   - \"Model\" \u2192 \"Core\" or \"Engine\"\n\n2. **Extract Sub-Orchestrators:**\n   - Move scheduling to a dedicated `SchedulingService`\n   - Move monitoring to a dedicated `MonitoringService`\n   - Keep `Orchestrator` as a thin coordinator\n\n3. **Introduce Event Bus:**\n   - Replace ad-hoc Observer Pattern with a centralized event bus\n   - Add event versioning for backwards compatibility\n\n4. **Adopt CQRS:**\n   - Separate write path (training, registration) from read path (dashboards, queries)\n   - Use eventual consistency for dashboard data\n\n5. **Remove Singleton:**\n   - Pass Orchestrator instance via dependency injection\n   - Enables isolated testing and multi-tenant scenarios\n\n---\n\n## 5. Conclusion\n\nThe LexiLearn MVC Orchestrator demonstrates a thoughtful application of the MVC pattern to an ML orchestration domain. The architecture provides clear separation of concerns, enables hot-swapping of ML strategies, and uses the Observer Pattern for loose coupling.\n\nHowever, the MVC metaphor is stretched in this context. The \"View\" is a data server, not a UI. The \"Controller\" has accumulated too many responsibilities. The manual Observer Pattern implementation in C lacks the elegance of framework-provided bindings.\n\nFor new team members, the key insights are:\n1. **Model = ML Logic + Data Persistence** \u2014 treat it as a library you call\n2. **Controller = Orchestration + Monitoring + Scheduling** \u2014 this is where decisions happen\n3. **View = External Communication** \u2014 REST/WebSocket gateway to dashboards\n4. **Communication = Function calls down, callbacks up**\n\nThe architecture is production-ready and has clearly been designed with MLOps principles in mind. Future improvements should focus on reducing Controller complexity and adopting patterns more native to event-driven backend systems.\n\n---\n\n## Appendix A: Key File References\n\n| Component | Header | Implementation |\n|-----------|--------|----------------|\n| Orchestrator | `src/controller/orchestrator.h` | `src/controller/orchestrator.c` |\n| Pipeline Manager | `src/controller/pipeline/pipeline_manager.h` | (impl in .c) |\n| Drift Detector | `src/controller/monitoring/drift_detector.h` | (header-only) |\n| Model Monitor | `src/controller/monitoring/model_monitor.h` | `src/controller/monitoring/model_monitor.c` |\n| Retraining Trigger | `src/controller/monitoring/retraining_trigger.h` | (header-only) |\n| Observer | `src/controller/monitoring/observer.h` | (header-only) |\n| Job Factory | `src/controller/job_factory/job_factory.h` | (impl in .c) |\n| Task Scheduler | `src/controller/scheduler/task_scheduler.h` | (impl in .c) |\n| Model Registry | `src/model/ml_pipeline/model_registry.h` | (impl in .c) |\n| Model Strategy | `src/model/ml_models/model_strategy.h` | (impl by concrete strategies) |\n| Dashboard Server | `src/view/dashboard_server.h` | (impl in .c) |\n\n## Appendix B: Design Pattern Summary\n\n| Pattern | Location | Purpose |\n|---------|----------|---------|\n| **MVC** | Entire architecture | Separation of concerns |\n| **Strategy** | `model_strategy.h` | Hot-swappable ML algorithms |\n| **Factory** | `job_factory.h` | Create diverse job types |\n| **Observer** | `observer.h` | Decouple event producers/consumers |\n| **Pipeline** | `pipeline_manager.h` | Orchestrate ETL \u2192 Train \u2192 Deploy |\n| **Singleton** | `orchestrator.c` | Global orchestrator instance (anti-pattern) |\n",

# LexiLearn MVC Orchestrator: Architectural Analysis and Critique

**Document Type:** Onboarding Guide for Senior Developers
**Version:** 1.0
**Author:** Architecture Team
**Date:** 2024

---

## Executive Summary

This document provides a definitive guide to the LexiLearn MVC Orchestrator's architecture, a C-based system for managing NLP/ML model pipelines with automated retraining, monitoring, and versioning. The system unconventionally applies the Model-View-Controller (MVC) pattern to an ML orchestration domain. This guide maps the components to MVC roles, describes communication pathways, traces a critical workflow, and provides a balanced architectural critique.

---

## 1. Component Mapping to MVC Roles

The LexiLearn Orchestrator implements a clear MVC pattern through its directory structure and component responsibilities. Below is the mapping with justifications:

### 1.1 Model Layer (`src/model/`)

The **Model** layer encapsulates all machine learning and data-related logic. It is completely agnostic to orchestration concerns and can operate independently.

| Directory/Component | File(s) | Purpose & Role |
|---------------------|---------|----------------|
| **Preprocessing** | `text_cleaner.{c,h}`, `tokenizer.{c,h}` | Text normalization and tokenization (BPE, WordPiece, SentencePiece) |
| **ML Models** | `model_strategy.h`, `transformer_summarizer.{c,h}`, `ngram_analyzer.{c,h}`, `hybrid_model.{c,h}` | Strategy Pattern implementations for pluggable algorithms |
| **ML Pipeline** | `model_trainer.{c,h}`, `model_evaluator.{c,h}`, `experiment_tracker.{c,h}` | Training orchestration, metrics computation, experiment tracking |
| **Model Registry** | `model_registry.{c,h}` | SQLite-backed versioning, lifecycle management (EXPERIMENT → STAGING → PRODUCTION → ARCHIVE
... (truncated)

      

      

        Bash Commands (12)
        
1. $ find /app/project -type f -name "*.c" -o -name "*.h" -o -name "*.md" | head -50
2. $ ls -la /app/project/
3. $ tree /app/project -L 3 -I "build|.git"
4. $ find /app/project/src -type d | sort
5. $ ls -la /app/project/src/controller/ && ls -la /app/project/src/model/ && ls -la /app/project/src/view/
6. $ find /app/project/src -type f \( -name "*.c" -o -name "*.h" \) | wc -l
7. $ find /app/project/src -type f \( -name "*.c" -o -name "*.h" \) | sort
8. $ ls -la /app/project/include/lexilearn/
9. $ ls -la /app/project/config/ && ls -la /app/project/docs/
10. $ find /app/project/src/model -type f -name "*.h" | xargs -I {} sh -c 'echo "=== {} ===" && head -30 {}'
11. $ head -50 /app/project/src/model/ml_pipeline/model_registry.c
12. $ mkdir -p /logs/agent
